                                 </msup>
                              </mrow>
                              <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }}} = {{R}^2}{{T}^2}/2{{A}^2}{{n}^4}{{F}^4}{{C}^2}{{\sigma }_{\mathrm{w}}}^2\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                           </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>where <i>R</i> and <i>T</i> are the gas constant (8.314 J mol<sup>−1</sup> K<sup>−1</sup>) and absolute temperature (298.15 K), respectively, and <i>A</i>, <i>n</i>, <i>F</i>, and <i>C</i> refer to the electrode surface area, a number of electrons involved in the electrochemical reaction, Faraday constant (96,485 C mol<sup>−1</sup>), and the sodium-ion concentration, respectively. The Warburg impedance coefficient (<i>σ</i><sub>w</sub>) is determined by the slope of the linear fitting of real impedance (Z′) versus ω<sup>−0.5</sup> plots in the Warburg term at low-frequency regions.</div>
               
               <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
                  <figure class="figure" id="advs9486-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6278cb85-c3eb-41fe-833f-5ddceba4c9fb/advs9486-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                           <source srcset="/cms/asset/6278cb85-c3eb-41fe-833f-5ddceba4c9fb/advs9486-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/cf583c04-e942-4abd-b8ff-8fd92b2b8e6d/advs9486-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6278cb85-c3eb-41fe-833f-5ddceba4c9fb/advs9486-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                        <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs9486-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.202408450" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                        </div>
                        <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">In situ EIS analysis of the Sn-based electrodes at various state-of-charge (SOC) conditions. Charge–discharge voltage profiles for the initial two cycles of the a) pure Sn/C and b) Sn@C/SiOC electrodes were measured at 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (≈0.07 C-rate) with voltage points where EIS was taken. Variation of the (c) total resistance (<i>R</i><sub>tot</sub>) and d) sodium-ion diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i><sub>Na⁺</sub>) values of the pure Sn/C and Sn@C/SiOC electrodes measured at voltage points indicated in a) and b). e) Schematic illustration of the sodiation/desodiation mechanisms of the pure Sn/C and Sn@C/SiOC electrodes. f) CV curves at different sweep rates (0.2–1.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>) and g) log <i>i</i> versus log <i>v</i> plots of the Sn@C/SiOC electrode (inset table: estimated b-values). h) Comparison of the relative contribution ratio of capacitive- and diffusion-controlled kinetics at various sweep rates (0.2–1.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>).</div>
                     </figcaption>
                  </figure>
               </section>
               <p>The changes in the <i>R</i><sub>tot</sub> and <i>D</i><sub>Na⁺</sub> values of the Sn/C and Sn@C/SiOC electrodes obtained from several SOCs during the initial two cycles are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0004">4c,d</a>, respectively. <i>R</i><sub>tot</sub> values of the Sn@C/SiOC electrode were lower compared to those of Sn/C at all SOC conditions, whereas both Sn-based electrodes exhibited similar variation trends for each parameter. Additionally, the Sn@C/SiOC electrode has higher overall <i>D</i><sub>Na⁺</sub> values than the pure Sn/C electrode under identical SOCs. This indicates that the sodium-ion transportation capability of Sn@C/SiOC is superior to that of the Sn/C electrode during battery operations. Moreover, as evident from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0004">4c,d</a>, a significant gap between two Sn-based electrodes is observed for both <i>R</i><sub>tot</sub> and <i>D</i><sub>Na⁺</sub> values during the alloying/dealloying reactions (yellow box area). Alloy-based anode materials, such as Si and Sn,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0056_R_d62622329e1356" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv. Energy Mater.">56</a>, <a href="#advs9486-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0057_R_d62622329e1356" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Energy Technol.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> have generally exhibited asymmetric alloying/dealloying behavior that originated mainly from a sluggish alloying step, which eventually causes poor rate performance. Compared to the desodiation process, the Sn/C electrode revealed higher <i>R</i><sub>tot</sub> and lower <i>D</i><sub>Na⁺</sub> values in sodiation, confirming that the Na<i>─</i>Sn alloying process is the rate-determining step for the sodiation/desodiation of the Sn anode. The Sn@C/SiOC electrode demonstrated substantially lower <i>R</i><sub>tot</sub> and higher <i>D</i><sub>Na⁺</sub> values compared to Sn/C, particularly in the first two cycles. Therefore, the realization of the hierarchical heterostructured nanohybrid composed of Sn yolk and C/SiOC shell provides a great boost for high-rate sodium-ion storage performance.</p>
               
               <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0004">4e</a> shows the different reaction mechanisms between the Sn/C and Sn@C/SiOC electrodes. For the Sn/C electrode, the sodiation gradually proceeds because of the slow diffusion kinetics without the porous ionic transport channels at the particle surface, whereas a relatively faster sodium-ion extraction can be achieved during desodiation. However, huge volume expansion/contraction of Sn causes undesirable surface cracking, pulverization of particles upon alloying/dealloying, and the generation of large Sn agglomerates after prolonged cycles,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0009_R_d62622329e1382" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Mater.">9</a>, <a href="#advs9486-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0012_R_d62622329e1382" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Nano Energy">12</a>, <a href="#advs9486-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0028_R_d62622329e1382" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Sci.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which may increase the effective diffusion distance and further interfere with redox reactions between sodium and Sn. For the Sn@C/SiOC electrode, the mesoporous and conductive C/SiOC shell offers a facile ionic transfer network at the particle surface, which facilitates the movement of sodium ions and ensures fast diffusion kinetics upon cycling. Furthermore, the mechanically and chemically stable C/SiOC shell relieves the internal mechanical stress arising from the large Sn yolk volume change and prevents the agglomeration of Sn particles and unfavorable side reactions between Sn and organic electrolyte, thereby enhancing the structural stability and electrochemical diffusion kinetics.</p>
               
               <div class="paragraph-element">The electrochemical kinetics of the Sn@C/SiOC electrode was investigated via CV tests at various scan rates (0.2–1.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>) to elucidate the reaction mechanism, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0004">4f</a>; and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13a</a> (Supporting Information). The charge storage mechanism of Sn consists of two kinetic factors, such as diffusion- and capacitive-controlled processes,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0058_R_d62622329e1398" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Adv. Energy Mater.">58</a>, <a href="#advs9486-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0059_R_d62622329e1398" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and their relative contributions can be quantified using Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs9486-disp-0002" title="Link to equation">2</a>)

                  <div class="inline-equation" id="advs9486-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                        <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/de816da5-56c8-4373-8758-f430627b9def/advs9486-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:21983844:media:advs9486:advs9486-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/advs9486-math-0002.png">
                           <semantics>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>log</mi>
                                 <mspace width="0.16em"></mspace>
                                 <mi>i</mi>
                                 <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                 <mi>log</mi>
                                 <mspace width="0.16em"></mspace>
                                 <mi>a</mi>
                                 <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                                 <mi>b</mi>
                                 <mspace width="0.16em"></mspace>
                                 <mi>log</mi>
                                 <mspace width="0.16em"></mspace>
                                 <mi>v</mi>
                              </mrow>
                              <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{log}}\,i = {\mathrm{log}}\,a + b\,{\mathrm{log}}\,v\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                           </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>where <i>v</i> is the sweep rate, <i>i</i> is the measured peak current, and <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are the empirical parameters. The <i>b</i>-values for each sodiation and desodiation process can be determined from the slope of the linear relationship of the log <i>i</i> versus log <i>v</i> plot, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0004">4g</a>; and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13b</a> (Supporting Information). Generally, the electrochemical reaction is dominated by surface capacitive behavior when the <i>b</i>-value is closer to 0.5, whereas the charge storage process is predominantly influenced by the diffusion-controlled faradaic behavior when the <i>b</i>-value is closer to 1.0.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0057_R_d62622329e1458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Energy Technol.">57</a>, <a href="#advs9486-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0059_R_d62622329e1458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The calculated <i>b</i>-values of the Sn@C/SiOC electrode are 0.61 and 0.76 for the oxidation and reduction steps, respectively, indicating combined diffusion-controlled and capacitive sodiation/desodiation behaviors (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0004">4g</a>). Conversely, the Sn/C electrode exhibits <i>b</i>-values of 0.5 and 0.61 for the oxidation and reduction reactions, respectively, revealing that most sodium ions can be stored through the diffusion-controlled process (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13b</a>, Supporting Information). In addition, the relative contribution ratios of capacitive- and diffusion-controlled kinetics at various sweep rates are calculated and summarized in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0004">4h</a> using Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs9486-disp-0003" title="Link to equation">3</a>)<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0033_R_d62622329e1480" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - ACS Nano">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
                  
                  <div class="inline-equation" id="advs9486-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                        <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/2bbb8199-e0b1-4959-9425-fde47c676051/advs9486-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:21983844:media:advs9486:advs9486-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/advs9486-math-0003.png">
                           <semantics>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>i</mi>
                                 <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                 <msub>
                                    <mi>k</mi>
                                    <mn>1</mn>
                                 </msub>
                                 <mi>v</mi>
                                 <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                                 <msub>
                                    <mi>k</mi>
                                    <mn>2</mn>
                                 </msub>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>v</mi>
                                    <mrow>
                                       <mn>1</mn>
                                       <mo>/</mo>
                                       <mn>2</mn>
                                    </mrow>
                                 </msup>
                              </mrow>
                              <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}i = {{k}_1}v + {{k}_2}{{v}^{1/2}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                           </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>the values of <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> <i>v</i> (capacitive-controlled) and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub> <i>v</i><sup>1/</sup><i><sup>2</sup></i> (diffusion-controlled) were determined by the measured current (<i>i</i>) and sweep rate (<i>v</i>) using Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs9486-disp-0003" title="Link to equation">3</a>). When the sweep rate was increased from 0.2 to 1.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, the capacitive-controlled contribution ratio increased from 49.5% to 69.7%. This result may be attributed to the mesoporous structure of the C/SiOC bilayer, which provides additional sodium-ion adsorption/desorption sites via capacitive-controlled kinetics, boosting sodium-ion storage characteristics even under fast charge/discharge conditions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0033_R_d62622329e1536" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - ACS Nano">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
               
               <p>Furthermore, as shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0005">5a</a>, the nanohybrid electrode demonstrates ultrastable cycling performance up to 1500 cycles even at a high current density of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (≈7 C-rate) with a remaining capacity of 421.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (retention: 91.9%), which is outstanding sodium-ion storage performances compared to the previous studies related to the Sn-based anodes for SIBs (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0060_R_d62622329e1558" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - J. Mater. Chem. A">60</a>-<a href="#advs9486-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0065_R_d62622329e1558" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - J. Power Sources">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> With the above physicochemical and electrochemical characterization, the reasons for obtaining excellent sodium-ion storage performance from the Sn@C/SiOC nanohybrid are summarized, as shown in the inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0005">5a</a>. First, through the sodiation and desodiation processes, the abundant void interspaces between the Sn yolk and C/SiOC bilayer shell inside the nanohybrid particles could effectively accommodate severe volume changes of Sn, leading to structural reinforcement and enhanced mechanical stability of the nanohybrid electrode. Second, the mesoporous and conductive C/SiOC shell facilitates the electrolyte's penetration into the inner Sn yolk and promotes the transport of sodium ions and electrons, ensuring fast sodium-ion diffusion kinetics and rapid redox reactions. Finally, this mesoporous C/SiOC structure provides additional sites for storing sodium ions through a capacitive reaction, enabling the fabrication of high-energy density anodes for SIBs.</p>
               
               <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
                  <figure class="figure" id="advs9486-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9ef8ff75-19d1-44b6-98da-cc4cacc9a452/advs9486-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                           <source srcset="/cms/asset/9ef8ff75-19d1-44b6-98da-cc4cacc9a452/advs9486-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/75ef72a6-ddd7-422f-9651-4d55365e7a40/advs9486-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9ef8ff75-19d1-44b6-98da-cc4cacc9a452/advs9486-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                        <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs9486-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.202408450" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                        </div>
                        <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Long-term cycling performance of the Sn@C/SiOC electrode at a current density of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and schematic of the combined effects of the multifunctional C/SiOC bilayer and yolk-shell nanohybrid structure (inset). b) Coin-type full-cell configuration consisting of Sn@C/SiOC as anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C as cathode. c) Galvanostatic charge–discharge voltage profiles for the 1st and 2nd cycles of the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C as cathode measured at 0.01&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>(≈0.1 C-rate, 1 C-rate for Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>: 117&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). d) Cycling performance of the full-cell at a current density of 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (≈10 C-rate).</div>
                     </figcaption>
                  </figure>
               </section>
            </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs9486-sec-0080">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="advs9486-sec-0080-title">2.3.3 Full-Cell Application</h4>
               
               <p>Finally, to confirm the potential application of the Sn@C/SiOC nanohybrid anode, a full-cell SIB was fabricated using Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C as the cathode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0005">5b</a>). Prior to fabrication, the Sn@C/SiOC electrode was precycled and presodiated, and the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C electrode also precycled in a half-cell condition. The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C cathode was prepared via the sol–gel method and demonstrates charge/discharge capacity of 103.0/100.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with 97.6% initial CE at a current density of 10&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#advs9486-fig-0005">5c</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs9486-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs9486-bib-0034_R_d62622329e1666" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Nano Res.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Sn@C/SiOC || Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C full-cell shows a reversible capacity of ≈60&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at a current density of 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with superior cycling stability over 400 cycles. Thus, the superior electrochemical performance of the Sn@C/SiOC nanohybrid in full-cell shed light on successful implementation of advanced SIB technology.</p>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="advs9486-sec-0090">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="advs9486-sec-0090-title">3 Conclusions</h2>
         
         <p>We synthesized the hierarchically designed yolk–shell Sn@C/SiOC via a facile pyrolysis technique for the first time to overcome the sluggish sodiation kinetics and massive volume changes of the Sn anode. The combined microstructural and morphological characterization results revealed that the Sn-based nanohybrids were composed of nanoscale Sn yolk particles with an interfacial SnO<i><sub>x</sub></i> nanolayer, encapsulated within a multifunctional C/SiOC bilayer shell. The unique, well-designed yolk–shell nanohybrid architecture provided abundant void interspaces between the nanosized Sn yolk and C/SiOC shell, mitigating large volume variations and enhancing the mechanical integrity and flexibility of the anode. Furthermore, the mesoporous C/SiOC bilayer further alleviated the massive volume change of Sn and enabled rapid sodium-ion diffusion, particularly during the sodiation process. Therefore, the Sn@C/SiOC electrodes demonstrated excellent sodium storage performance in terms of high reversible capacity (521&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), superior rate capability (up to 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and ultrastable cycling performance (5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 91.1% even after 1500 cycles). The Sn@C/SiOC || Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C full-cell with highly stable sodium-ion storage performance over 400 cycles further demonstrates the practical high applicability of the high-capacity anode. The simple and facile synthetic procedure and hierarchical design approach based on the proposed yolk–shell heterostructure offer valuable insights into the development of various electrode materials for secondary batteries and energy storage devices.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
